Important News

Hsi-Chia and Japan 81

Rumors of Secret Agreements Negotiated

The Loss of Kirin in One Fell Swoop

A correspondent in Beiping reports that according to those newly returning to Beiping from Kirin, after the Japanese army occupied Jilin, they greatly encouraged Hsi-Chia, as he was a banner man, a member of the Manchu imperial family, and a student of General Muto (during his studies at the Japanese Military Academy). Initially, Hsi was still somewhat apprehensive and dared not accept. The Japanese, on the one hand, used force to pressure him, and on the other hand, used kind words to persuade him, tempting him with benefits and seducing him with women, lavishly flattering him in every way, even more so than they treated Li Wanyong, the Korean traitor at the time. Hsi-Chia was overwhelmed by the favor and became ecstatic, gradually no longer caring about anything else and resolutely declaring independence. The Japanese machinations and methods are truly astonishing. When the Japanese army first entered Jilin, their targets included not only Hsi-Chia but also Rong Hou, the Director of Finance, as both were banner men. However, Rong Hou had different intentions. After hearing about the Shenyang Incident on September 19, he advocated resistance to the Japanese army. Hsi-Chia refused, saying that his superiors had instructed him to take a non-resistance approach and that soldiers should obey orders and not act freely. Seeing that Hsi would not listen, Rong Hou knew that he was timid and unable to take on the responsibility. He immediately counted and handed over two million yuan in cash from the Kirin provincial treasury to Hsi-Chia, saying that he had been Director of Finance for eight years and that outsiders misunderstood, saying that he had filled his own pockets. In reality, he was still penniless. What he could take comfort in was that the savings of Kirin province were now several million in cash, which had been accumulated over the years from the profits of the Yongheng Official Bank's mining and forestry businesses. Now, he was handing them over to him, and he should make good use of them. After handing over the funds, he immediately resigned and fled, hurrying to Harbin within a day. On the morning of the 21st at 6:00 AM, the Japanese army confiscated the weapons of the police departments of the Jichang and Jidun Railways in Changchun. At 10:00 AM, after the matter was completed, they boarded the train and went straight to Jilin. Upon receiving the news, Hsi-Chia urgently summoned representatives from various legal entities to welcome the Japanese army at Jiuzhan (the third station west of Jilin). Hsi also personally went to the station, bowing and scraping to greet the Japanese army. When the Japanese army arrived, the leader was Muto. The meeting of the teacher and student somewhat reduced Hsi's trembling state. After entering the city, Muto learned that Rong Hou had left and saw that Hsi-Chia was easily deceived. He first used pressure tactics, ordering him to hand over all the weapons of the provincial garrison and the police. Hsi requested an extension because it was late at night. The next morning, he handed over more than 500 rifles and some ammunition. Muto was dissatisfied with the small amount and scolded him, ordering him to search again. Hsi then collected more than 1,000 rifles, and Muto was slightly satisfied, changing his pressure tactics and adopting a policy of appeasement. Rumors that we once threatened each other with guns and detained Hsi for several hours are all rumors and are not credible. Seeing that Muto treated him with courtesy and offered all kinds of inducements, Hsi regarded Muto as his benefactor. From then on, Hsi listened to everything and followed every plan. Seeing that Hsi had already fallen into his trap, Muto proceeded to induce him to declare independence and also requested Liaoning to declare independence, which was no longer a problem. In the future, the new regime in the Northeast would definitely be acquired by the restoration faction. Puyi was already on his way, and Prince Gong and Prince Su were also on their way. You are a member of the imperial family and have made great contributions. I will use my influence as your teacher to guarantee that the real power in Kirin province will belong to you. Hearing this, Hsi was still slightly hesitant, fearing that Zhang and Liang would return to Shenyang and that Zhang Zuoxiang would return to his homeland. At that time, he would miscalculate. Knowing his intentions, Muto further incited him, saying that the two Zhangs had no hope of returning. If the restoration fails, the Japanese army will permanently occupy the three provinces. Even if you want to save yourself, I can hardly guarantee it, let alone your position. After this incitement, Hsi's mind was greatly made up, and the act of independence was realized on September 30. Seeing that Hsi had declared independence and his mission was accomplished, Muto immediately returned to Shenyang and dispatched Colonel Tsuboi as the Jilin Garrison Commander. All administrative matters were carried out under his command. However, he treated Hsi-Chia with the utmost respect in private, and within a few days, he presented Hsi with two courtesans, nominally as concubines, but in reality, to secretly monitor his actions. Money was used according to Hsi's wishes, without any reservations. However, when it came to official matters, he immediately put on a stern face and refused to budge. As a result, Hsi enjoyed more freedom in private than in any other era, but he had no real power at all. Since the beginning of this month, newspapers in China have criticized Hsi for betraying the country, and telegrams from all sides have been pouring in, severely condemning him. Although Hsi was unable to read them all, he occasionally caught a glimpse of one or two, and people were constantly whispering that Hsi Er Ye (Hsi Xing Er), what he had done, was deeply hated by all parties in Beiping and Nanjing. These words reached Hsi's ears, and he became wary again. On the one hand, he issued orders to the counties one after another, subtly explaining his difficulties and asking for understanding. On the other hand, he bought off former "piglet" parliamentarians, giving them titles such as advisors and consultants, sending them to the counties to preach his virtues. The generally unscrupulous parliamentarians seized this opportunity and rushed to their respective destinations with joy. However, most of the counties refused to obey because Hsi had already betrayed the country and had no real power. In particular, the actual power was held by the garrison commanders of Jichang, Yilan, Yanji, Binjiang, Suining, and Wuzhen, who refused to obey Hsi's orders. Hsi's plan was exhausted. He was forced to secretly discuss with the Japanese side, promising favorable terms to make the Japanese side recognize Zhang Zuoxiang as co-governor of Jilin, as a means of currying favor with Zhang Zuoxiang and demonstrating his support. It is said that the Japanese side was represented in this meeting by Mitsujo, the chief writer of the Dongbao and advisor to the Jilin Japanese Army Garrison Command. After three days of consultation, an agreement was reached. At 3:00 PM on October 18, Hsi-Chia held a grand banquet for his guests at the Provincial Government. Those present from the Japanese side included Commander Muto, Garrison Commander Yano (Tsuboi had left his post), Commander of the Military Police Ohtani Risaburo, Japanese Consul Ishisha Dairo, and Mr. Mitsujo. From the Chinese side, there were Zhang Jietou, Chairman of the Jilin Provincial Chamber of Commerce, Xie Guanglin, Chairman of the Farmers' Association, Jiang Dafeng, Chairman of the Labor Union, and Han Shiqing and Zhang Shousan, Chairmen of the Education Association, etc. Amidst laughter and merriment, the agreement was formally signed. At that time, from the Governor's Office to Henan Street, sentries, cavalry, machine gun squads, and plainclothes detectives were densely deployed. The situation was tense, as if facing a formidable enemy. The state of emergency lasted until 6:00 PM. The contents of the secret agreement, as heard, are recorded below:

1. The Jihui Railway shall be completed within three months, with simultaneous construction starting from Yanji and Dunhua, and it shall be converted to double track.

2. Japan shall have the right to designate land for purchase throughout Kirin Province.

3. The commercial ports (Jilin and Changchun) shall be leased in perpetuity.

Zhang Haipeng's Plot to Attack Longjiang: A Detailed Account 82

The Heilongjiang Army Strictly Refuses Zhang, His Plan Thwarted

Zhang's Troops Defect, Causing Division

The Japanese Consul in Heilongjiang Moves to Harbin

Harbin Correspondence: Now that the Japanese have occupied Liaoning and Jilin provinces, they are eager to annex Longjiang. However, their public declarations state that their scope is limited to the South Manchurian Railway zone. Since Longjiang is located in northern Manchuria, there is no reason to send troops. Thus, they employed sinister schemes, using Chinese traitors as their pawns, while they remained behind the scenes, issuing orders. Zhang Haipeng, the traitor and garrison commander of Taonan, whose courtesy name is Xiantao, came from a bandit background. Although he is nearly seventy years old and holds a high official position, his ambition is still frequently revealed in his words. When Wan Fulin was in charge of Longjiang, during the time when Yang Yuting and Chang Yinhuai were executed and political turmoil was stirring, Zhang had long harbored the intention of seizing power. He had secretly allied with a certain high official, planning to coordinate actions. However, the high official changed his mind at the last moment and remained idle. Zhang realized that his own forces were too weak and ultimately did not dare to launch an attack. Although this matter was quelled before it could happen, everyone knew his intentions. The Japanese noticed his hidden desires and knew that Zhang's fourth son was usually associated with bandits and commanded more than two thousand men, acting lawlessly. They could easily use profit and desire to manipulate him. This is the reason why the Japanese enticed Zhang to become a traitor. I will now describe it in detail as follows:

First, a Japanese man named Tomosaburo, claiming to be acting under the order of the Kwantung Army Commander, visited Zhang and asked him to take charge, promising that everything in Liaoning Province would be supported by the Japanese. Zhang initially hesitated because a certain military officer under his command advised him against it, fearing he would fall into the Japanese trap. Therefore, he did not give a clear answer at the time. Not many days after Tomosaburo left, a Japanese army major named Oishi, carrying the Kwantung Army Commander's calling card and a letter of introduction, said that he had secret matters to discuss in person and requested an audience. The major told Zhang, "Currently, most of the key officials in the three northeastern provinces have left their posts. Among the senior military officers, only Your Excellency is the most respected and esteemed. Not only does our Commander admire you, but even the Emperor knows Your Excellency's prestige. Therefore, our army now wants to invite Your Excellency to take the position of Chairman of Jiang Province. Our army will fully provide all the military equipment and supplies needed." Although Zhang remained ambiguous and evasive, the major had already discerned his intentions. Therefore, after the major left, he secretly promised Zhang's fourth son a large sum of money as an inducement. A few days later, the Japanese suddenly transported two trainloads of military weapons and ammunition, which stopped at Taonan Station. Zhang was not initially aware of this. When he sent a representative to the train to inquire with the Japanese, they falsely claimed that the weapons were being transported to the Mongolian Youth League and that they would immediately confiscate the weapons of the reclamation army because the mastermind of the Nakamura incident, although not part of this force, was still part of the reclamation army. Zhang clearly knew that the Japanese had ulterior motives and were using this trick as a tool for coercion. Therefore, he decided to play along, demanding that the Japanese hand over the two trainloads of weapons to him. The Japanese agreed. Zhang also telegraphed Vice Commander Zhang and Chairman Wan about this matter. Zhang felt self-satisfied, thinking that he had obtained a large amount of weapons without effort (these weapons were stolen by the Japanese from the Liaoning Arsenal), which would allow him to increase his military strength and consolidate his position. However, things did not go as planned. Within a few days, the Japanese repeatedly urged Zhang to send troops to attack Jiang Province, pressing him aggressively. At this time, Zhang had already realized that he had fallen into the Japanese trap, but it was too late to regret and there was no way to escape. He had no choice but to send a special envoy to report the situation to the military and political authorities, requesting their understanding. After a week of back-and-forth consultations, the provincial authorities, realizing that Zhang's intentions were set and irreversible and knowing that the Japanese would follow him, feared that any armed resistance would lead to a repeat of the Jinzhou tragedy, causing great losses to the people and devastating the region. Therefore, they convened an emergency meeting. Some military personnel advocated for war, while Chief of Staff Xie Ke strongly advocated for peace. In this critical situation, they preferred to act pragmatically rather than stick to the rules and take responsibility themselves. Once the decision was made, they issued an order on the spot, notifying the front lines to withdraw their defenses. Meanwhile, representatives from various legal entities took a special train to Taonan to welcome Zhang, with the attached request that Zhang follow public opinion and postpone his arrival in Jiang for two or three days so that the troops in various locations could be transferred in an orderly manner to prevent any contact or accidental clashes in the meantime. After the delegation left, they received an urgent telegram from Bei'an that same evening, ordering them not to retreat and to do their utmost to stop Zhang, even if it meant defending with all their strength, down to the last soldier. At the same time, there was a telegram appointing Ma Zhanshan (then the Heihe Garrison Commander) as Chairman of the Jiang Province government, with a clause stating that he would also serve as Commander-in-Chief in the event of war. At this point, the morale of the troops suddenly rose and their momentum increased greatly. They immediately increased the deployment of troops and headed to Jiangqiao (about 120 li from the provincial capital) and other places to keep Zhang's troops in check from a distance. At this time, Zhang had already arrived in the province on the delegation's special train. When he arrived in Tailai County, he learned that the situation had changed drastically and that the Jiangqiao (originally a wooden bridge more than a li long) had been blown up and was impassable. Zhang immediately turned back, leaving only a small vanguard force behind, which did not have time to retreat and therefore had some conflict with the provincial army. On the 15th, a Japanese plane flew over, a small plane that circled the provincial capital four times. At times, it flew very low, only a few dozen feet from the rooftops. Those looking up from below could clearly see two people on board, one of whom was constantly looking down through binoculars. The fuselage was gray, with the number 87. Each wing had a sun-shaped mark with a red circle. It did not drop any bombs but dropped a package over the Japanese consulate, presumably containing important documents that could not be sent by mail. It then flew away. The 16th was the day scheduled for war against Zhang. The citizens were extremely frightened, fearing that planes would come to intimidate the province. Fortunately, there was wind and rain all day long, and the planes did not appear. On the 17th, there were also no signs of planes. On the 18th, a plane flew in from the Taonan area. It looked similar to the one that had come before, but this time it flew very high and only circled the provincial capital once before flying southwest (in the direction of South Manchuria). It is speculated that the reason it did not dare to fly low was perhaps because on the 16th, near Tailai County, four Japanese planes dropped bombs, one of which was shot down by our army with artillery, wounding one Japanese and capturing another. Furthermore, on the 17th, the Heihe Military Police Enforcement Office posted a notice stating that in the future, any Japanese planes or planes from Zhang's rebel army that came to the provincial capital would be shot down with anti-aircraft guns, and merchants and residents should not panic. The Japanese may have learned of this news, which is why the plane that came today was so cautious. It is also possible. Currently, the military strength in Jiang Province totals four brigades, all under the command of Ma Zhanshan. The military resources are abundant and sufficient for deployment. Furthermore, according to reliable reports, Xu and Zhang's regiments under Zhang's command, deeply understanding the greater good, have defected and launched a counter-offensive. Therefore, Zhang's internal forces are now divided and in disarray. Although the Japanese army is providing support from behind, it is unlikely to be of any use. It is truly a case of collapsing without being attacked. Zhang's eldest son currently occupies the position of Director of the Tao'an Railway Bureau. Although the reclamation army is also under his control, fortunately, there are many who can distinguish right from wrong in the army and will not be loyal to Zhang. Currently, a portion of Regiment Commander Zhu's troops no longer obey Zhang's orders and have automatically retreated to the Jingxing area. Currently, the Japanese consulate and the South Manchuria Railway office in the provincial capital are empty. All of them left the provincial capital for Harbin three days ago. Before leaving, the Japanese consul sent a letter to Chief of Staff Xie Ke of the Military Headquarters, thanking him for the hospitality. The Korean residents were also given travel expenses by the Japanese consulate to go to Harbin. Only a small number of those not on the Japanese consulate's list, like stray dogs, had nowhere to go. However, these people all relied on opium dens for a living and were usually acquainted with lower-class vagrants, so they were still able to hide temporarily.

Wuhu All Circles Sever Relations with Japan 83

Many Chinese Employees of Japanese Stores Resign Voluntarily

Legal and Education Circles Telegraph Request for Declaration of War

Wuhu Correspondence: Since the Japanese invasion and occupation of the three northeastern provinces, all circles in Wuhu have been extremely indignant. All schools immediately implemented military training and organized propaganda teams, first promoting in the urban area and now moving to rural areas. The theaters, due to the drop in water levels, are scheduled to resume screenings on the first of next month and have been ordered to select more adventurous and patriotic films to stimulate the people's enthusiasm for saving the country. The volunteer army initiated and organized by the education circle has applied to the volunteer army committee of all circles for registration. The volunteer army preparatory committees of the chambers of commerce and various trade associations have also elected Tao Yudang, Chen Shaotang, and Xu Xinpu as director and deputy directors, respectively, and will apply for organization soon. The regulations are drafted in accordance with the Shanghai volunteer army's measures. Staff members of the county party headquarters and the public security bureau still take turns giving public speeches at the YMCA every night to resist Japan and save the country. Sun Huaxin, the executive of the student department of the Liaoning YMCA, recently came to Wuhu to report to all circles the various atrocities he witnessed committed by the Japanese. Everyone who heard it was filled with indignation. In recent days, schools such as the Senior Elementary School, No. 2 Girls' Middle School, No. 7 Middle School, No. 1 Vocational School, and the Guangyi Elementary School of the Wuhu Customs have all invited Sun to give lectures on national humiliation to expand their deep understanding of Japan. The various middle schools have recently initiated the organization of a joint anti-Japanese national salvation association, planning to publicly elect representatives to go to the capital to attend the national student anti-Japanese representative conference. The various elementary schools have initiated the saving of candy money for national salvation, estimating that 300 yuan can be obtained each month. Due to the continuation of Japanese military atrocities, the business community is filled with indignation and believes that only economic severance can control the lives of the Japanese. They will comply with the anti-Japanese meeting resolution to seal up Japanese goods and order all stores to print anti-Japanese slogans on advertising paper. Although the mining coal is under contract with Japanese ships and cannot be transported to Wuhu to supply factories with small boats, other mining coal can still be transported to replace it. All Chinese who work on Japanese ships and in Japanese stores have voluntarily resigned to express their spirit of non-cooperation. The dare-to-die corps of party members is being organized. The county party headquarters is being partially reorganized and will strengthen the anti-Japanese work to unify the anti-Japanese steps and handle rapeseed registration. Shibata Shirao, the Japanese consul stationed in Wuhu, has recently changed to using Japanese in documents exchanged with the county government. County magistrate Yu Yuying, believing that his etiquette was improper and violated international practice, sent a letter back requesting him to respect the main body and change to using Chinese. Furthermore, a small boat of the Mitsubishi Company of Japan recently struck and killed Fu Xiaohuzi, who was engaged in singing for a living. The court sent a prosecutor to examine the body, and the public security bureau and the county government separately sent personnel to investigate and will present a negotiation to the Japanese consul. The anti-Japanese associations of the various county schools and the lawyers' association believe that the Japanese are intentionally provoking in the Yangtze River area and have separately telegraphed the central national government, requesting severance of diplomatic relations with Japan and the speedy declaration of war. Their anger is very strong, which shows the prosperity of the popular spirit in Wuhu. (October 25th)

Hankou's Japanese Tai'an Yarn Factory Closes Voluntarily 84

The Japanese Consul in Hankou Sends a Letter to the Police Department to Intimidate

Unemployed Workers Petition the City Government for Relief

All Yangtze River Japanese Ships Will Cease Operations

Hankou Correspondence: The Tai'an Yarn Factory, opened by Japanese merchants in Hankou, closed voluntarily on the 16th of this month, citing the Chinese boycott movement, causing thousands of Chinese workers to become unemployed suddenly. In the ten days since the factory closed, the unemployed workers have never made excessive demands on the factory and have tried their best to avoid disorderly actions. However, the Japanese made unfounded remarks, saying that the workers would face severe consequences. Therefore, on the 26th, the factory was closed, and the Japanese Consul-General sent a letter to the Garrison Headquarters requesting protection, which was close to intimidation. After receiving the letter, the Police Department immediately sent a reply refuting it and ordered Battalion Commander Fan to strengthen protection. However, after the factory closed, thousands of workers were completely released from the factory. The labor-management issues are being handled by the City Party Headquarters, the City Government, and the City Federation of Trade Unions, trying their best to avoid direct negotiations between the workers and the factory. However, because the workers suddenly became unemployed, and it was extremely difficult to make a living after the floods, they elected Yu Shaoqing, Cui Haitao, Guo Yushan, Pi Yishan, and Zhang Shanzhi as representatives to petition the City Government. Mayor He Baohua was out on official business, so He Diqin met with them instead, but there were no results. On the 27th, the representatives went to the City Government again. He Baohua met with them in person. The worker representatives first described the process of the Tai'an Yarn Factory's voluntary shutdown and closure, as well as the difficult living conditions of the workers after their unemployment, and requested relief, and put forward three requests: (1) Request the Tai'an Yarn Factory to pay severance pay for six months, and reply within three days; (2) Before the severance pay is resolved, the factory should pay each worker a daily living allowance of four dimes a day; (3) Request the City Government to find ways to place the workers so that they will not be unemployed. Mayor He replied that he would negotiate with the Japanese consul regarding the severance pay, the government would temporarily advance the living allowance, and he would try his best to find jobs. The worker representatives, satisfied with the reply, left the City Government and notified the workers to wait quietly for a resolution. Regarding the second request, the City Government immediately advanced the funds that day and distributed them together with the Party Headquarters and the Trade Union to temporarily maintain the lives of the workers.

In other news, since the Mukden Incident, all circles here have been filled with grief and indignation. Therefore, no one patronizes the Japanese shipping company Nisshin Kisen's Yangtze River ships, which are about to cease all operations. Ships such as the Dayuan, Dali, Daji, and Dafu on the Shanghai-Hankou route, Daheng on the Hankou-Yichang route, and Wuling on the Hankou-Changsha route have no passengers or cargo to carry, whether upstream or downstream. Currently, most of the stewards on these ships have returned to their hometowns, and all the sailors and pilots have also voluntarily resigned. It is rumored that the company intends to lease all of its Yangtze River ships to British merchants to manage on their behalf, but the British merchants fear causing resentment among the Chinese and have not dared to accept. (October 27th)

Guangdong Province Ends Hunan's Miscellaneous Troops 85

Chen Chuliang's Troops Dissolved

Yan Renyi's Troops Reorganized

Guangzhou Correspondence: When the Guangdong-Guangxi armies entered Hunan some time ago, Tang Shengzhi had reorganized several brigades of Hunan's miscellaneous troops, handing them over to Chen Jitang to be incorporated into the First Army Corps as pioneers for entering Hengzhou, Hunan. The troops of Chen Tiejian, Zhao Zixin, Yan Renyi, and Chen Chuliang had successively approached Hengzhou. Before long, the proposal for peaceful unification arose, and the Guangdong-Guangxi armies returned. The troops that had advanced deep into the vicinity of Hengzhou were intercepted by the Hunan He-faction troops and suffered some losses. The remaining troops, led by Yan Renyi and Chen Chuliang, retreated to the area of Pingshi and Lechang on the Guangdong border. Later, because the newly formed army had poor discipline, causing discontent among the local people, they filed a complaint with the First Army Corps Headquarters. The Headquarters secretly ordered the troops of the 7th Division of the 3rd Army, stationed in Lechang, commanded by Huang Yanzhen, to dispatch a team to Dongtou Street on the evening of the 15th of this month, surrounding and disarming Chen's troops. Regiment Commander Zhou Yunshan fled in fear of punishment. The officers and soldiers of his command were all repatriated to their hometowns by the 7th Division. However, since Chen Chuliang had not committed any illegal acts, the First Army Corps appointed him as the commander of the directly subordinate 7th Brigade, allowing him to recruit and form an army anew. Furthermore, the troops of Yan Renyi's newly formed 1st Division, currently stationed in Chenzhou, are also being reorganized. Yan Renyi telegraphed the Headquarters yesterday, requesting that the name of the newly formed 1st Division be canceled and that the Division Headquarters, as well as the officers and cadets, and the 1st battalion of infantry under his command, be assigned to other units or disbanded. After receiving the report, Chen Jitang quickly approved the cancellation of the Division's name and ordered that his troops be received and reorganized by Gong Hao (Gong is currently serving as a commander in a certain army of the Fourth Army Corps). The pay for this unit, starting from November, will be received directly by Gong from the National Government. At the same time, he sent a telegram to Guangxi Province, ordering Gong to be notified and handle the matter. (October 23rd)

Local Correspondence

Songjiang 86

Tang's Murder Case Investigation: Family Members and the County Public Security Bureau Capture Thief Shen Shaoqing, who revealed clues about the tragic murder of Tang Zhikui, the owner of the Tang Helong oil and sesame store last year, implicating his son Tang Daguan as having instigated the murder. The prosecutor's office immediately summoned the deceased's son Tang Qiusheng and apprentices for investigation, with strict security measures. Tang Qiusheng is currently detained in the detention center with strict restrictions on visitation. Today (28th) at 2:00 PM, Prosecutor Ren led a clerk and two bailiffs to Tang Zhikui's house across the Kuayu Bridge to reinvestigate, drawing detailed diagrams of the deceased's bedroom and routes of entry and exit for reference. They also ordered the deceased's family members Tang Zhigao and Tang Jingren, as well as apprentice Zhang Xidi, to be brought back for interrogation. The contents are detailed, but Tang Jingren is suspected of smoking opium and has been sent to Songjiang Hospital for testing. Tang Zhigao and Zhang Xidi were ordered to return to await further investigation.

The Volunteer Army Committee Establishes an Anti-Japanese National Salvation Association: Following the recommendation of the County Chamber of Commerce, the organization of the Volunteer Army Committee has been previously discussed at the standing committee. Representatives from the garrison, the Party Headquarters, the County Government, the First District Office, various middle schools, the Chamber of Commerce, and the Fire Brigade, totaling thirteen members, convened the first meeting of the Volunteer Army Committee. Chen Jing, the principal of the Provincial Normal School, Shi Heng, the standing member of the County Party Headquarters, and Cai Zhongyu, the chairman of the County Chamber of Commerce, were elected as standing committee members. Zhong Taichi of the First District Office was instructed to draft the organizational regulations of the Volunteer Army Committee and start work immediately. The office is attached to the County Party Headquarters.

Fengxian 87

Water Patrol Commander under Police Team Command: Water Patrol Captain Ding Zhiyan has stated that, according to regulations, the water patrol team is an independent entity. It is unclear whether it can be commanded by the police team. He has requested the County Government to telegraph the Provincial Government for instructions. It has been learned that the Provincial Civil Affairs Department has already sent instructions to the county, stating that the newly formed water patrol team in the county is small in number and there is no need to set up a separate team headquarters. The police team leader should still be in charge of command and deployment to be fiscally efficient.

Robbery Occurs at Wuwai Fifty-seven: Last night, more than 20 bandits speaking the Chongming dialect suddenly surrounded the house of resident Tang Zixiang in the Fifty-seventh district of Wuwai, forced their way in, tied up the entire family, and ransacked the house. Before leaving, they carried away a full load of Huami (millet). By the time neighbors discovered the robbery and went to pursue them, they had already fled far away.

Suzhou 88

Farmhouse in Lishu Township Robbed: At around 10:00 PM on the night before last (26th), eight bandits speaking with a foreign accent and armed with handguns suddenly broke into the home of Lu Yongfu, a resident of Xiatali in the second district of Lishu Township. After looting, they fled towards the Daidai Bridge area, stealing clothing and other items worth several hundred yuan.

Wuxi 89

Land Tax for Road Construction Transferred to Public Works Relief: The Wuxi Flood Relief Association held its sixth meeting of executives, directors, and standing committee members yesterday, chaired by Qian Sunqing. Key decisions were made. First, the three thousand yuan of the land tax for road construction, previously deposited in the Bank of Communications, has been transferred to dike repair and public works relief. The Construction Bureau cannot use this money without the association's notification. Li Tiping, Hua Yisan, Chen Zhanru, and Tu Keqiang were appointed to petition the province, requesting approval of the county council's decision to transfer the five thousand yuan of land tax for road construction to dike repair and public works relief, so that work can begin. Second, the provincial departments should requisition ships to rescue flood victims in northern Jiangsu, and all expenses should be allocated from the northern Jiangsu relief fund. The Chamber of Commerce should send a letter to the Shanghai Flood Relief Association for review and approval. Third, another thousand yuan of relief funds should be allocated to Gaochun.

Jiangyin 90

Finance and Agriculture Departments Inspect Damaged Crops: Chen Naidong of the Finance Department and Dai Xi of the Agriculture and Mining Department were ordered to come to Cheng the day before yesterday to inspect the crop damage in all districts. They have completed their work. Yesterday (26th), they held a meeting at the county government. After discussion, according to the original report on disaster fields, a total of 327,455 acres of farmland in the county were damaged. A total of 97,231 acres of Cao Tian and 1,256 acres of Shatian in the Sixth District were completely destroyed. The actual number of acres that were inundated was only about 30%, which is seven-tenths less than the original reported number.

Acting Principal of Nanjing Middle School Arrives in Cheng: The position of principal of Nanjing Middle School has been vacant for a long time. After the Department of Education appointed Zhang Yiyan to the position, some of the students opposed him. Zhang, after accepting the appointment, came to Cheng on the 26th with Yuan Jianhan and Yang Xiangting and stayed at the Huayuan Hotel. According to Zhang, the Department of Education ordered him to act as principal for three or four weeks and then return to Nantong. To take over the school, two points must be resolved: (1) Wait for the school board member Chen Gucen to come to Cheng to discuss the school's financial problems so that it can be sustained; (2) Whether the school board can produce a new principal in the shortest possible time. If it is delayed for four weeks, I will find it difficult to maintain the position for a long time. Therefore, the takeover has not been scheduled.

Changzhou 91

Victim of Vandalism Dies: A group of merchants in Wujin vandalized the county party headquarters and other institutions, and Assistant Secretary Wu Wenbi of the party was injured. Doctors Lick and Zhu Luzhong of Jinren Hospital in Wuxi came to Changzhou to perform a joint operation on Wu's head with Dr. Bei De, the director of the Wujin Hospital, removing bone fragments and necrotic tissue. However, the injury was still severe, and Wu died in the hospital at 4:00 AM on the 28th. Wu was 24 years old, his parents were deceased, and he had an older brother and a younger sister. His wife's maiden name was Sun, and they each had a child. The various institutions are now handling the funeral arrangements.

County Court to be Reorganized: Lei Renlong, the president of the Wujin County Court, and Yang Kongyi, the chief prosecutor, believed that Wujin had too many lawsuits and jointly proposed reorganizing the county court into a district court. They submitted the proposal to the High Court for review. Yesterday, an order was received stating that the reorganization was too simple and that the county court should be temporarily reorganized into a Wujin branch of the Wuxi District Court, which would be more practical. The Jiangdu County Court has been reorganized into a district branch and the Ministry of Justice has already approved the report. The existing plan should be used, and the Jiangdu case should be used as a reference to create a reorganization of the district branch and formulate a budget for review.

Nantong 92

High Court Thoroughly Investigates Opium Burning Scandal: The High Court sent Wang Sixian, a prosecutor from the Shanghai District Court, to Nantong to thoroughly investigate the County Court's opium burning scandal. According to the investigation, the missing and replaced opium were mostly still sealed, and it should be determined whether administrative or judicial personnel are responsible. The High Court should review it. The prosecutor's office will continue to investigate the inside details of the case. The Chamber of Commerce Deals with the Aftermath of Japanese Goods: Japanese goods in Nantong stores have all been sealed up, causing financial turmoil in the market in recent days. On the 27th, the Chamber of Commerce called a meeting of representatives from various industries to discuss the aftermath. In addition to the Chamber of Commerce negotiating with the silver and money industries to coordinate a solution, it also submitted a request to the province for assistance.

Hangzhou 93

The second preparatory meeting was held last night. Bandits Rampant in Wenling and Yuhuan: The Zhejiang Provincial Government reported that bandits led by Fang Yi and Cheng Hongfa had gathered crowds in Maoyu and Maotan, bordering Wenling and Yuhuan, and looted the villages, burning down more than a hundred houses. After receiving the report, the Provincial Government urgently telegraphed the two county governments to cooperate and immediately ordered Zhu Bingxi, the commander of the 4th Security Regiment, to lead his troops to suppress the bandits.

Second Preliminary Meeting of Beijing and Guangdong Representatives Held Yesterday 94

Focusing on Discussing Unified Foreign Policy

Specific Measures Have Been Decided, But Not Yet Released

Negotiations to be Handled by the Nanjing Government

Decisions on Proposals to be Made by the Central Party Headquarters of Both Sides

The Beijing and Guangdong representatives held their second preliminary meeting at 10:00 AM yesterday, again at Mr. Wu's residence on Gordon Road. Li Shizeng arrived in Shanghai at 8:10 AM yesterday morning, having taken the night express train from Beijing, and immediately rushed to attend the meeting. Wu Tiecheng initially represented Li in attendance, but after Li himself arrived, Wu left the meeting at around 11:00 AM. The remaining representatives continued the meeting until it adjourned at 12:00 PM. Yesterday's meeting focused on foreign affairs, and it was decided that future discussions regarding foreign policy and principles would take place in the representatives' meetings, while the Nanjing government would be responsible for conducting negotiations. Other internal affairs will be discussed starting in the third preliminary meeting this morning.

Major Issues Decided Yesterday. After the second preliminary meeting adjourned yesterday, the interim chairman Wang Jingwei issued the following results in writing: The second meeting was held at Mr. Wu's residence on Gordon Road at 10:00 AM on October 28th. Those present were Wang Zhaoming, Li Yuying, Zhang Ji, Zhang Jingjiang, Cai Yuanpei, Li Wenfan, Wu Chaoshu, Sun Ke, Chen Youren, Zou Lu, Wu Tiecheng, and Chen Mingshu. Wang Zhaoming was the chairman, and Zhong Tianxin, Qiu Jinxian, Yang Zongjiong, and Cheng Zhonghang were the recorders. Formalities were observed as usual. The resolutions were: (1) The purpose of this meeting is to discuss methods and formulate specific plans, with the final decision-making power residing in the Central Party Headquarters of both sides. (2) Regarding foreign affairs, the Nanjing government will be responsible for conducting negotiations, while the direction and principles will be discussed in this meeting and reported at any time, without being released to the outside world unless necessary. (3) Reply to the letter from the Capital's Anti-Japanese National Salvation Association (original attached). Today's meeting was based on the seven items proposed in the letter from the Guangdong representatives to Mr. Chiang Kai-shek, focusing on the first item regarding unified foreign policy. Various specific measures have been determined, but due to time constraints, they are temporarily inconvenient to release. Discussions The entire delegation

expressed their firm commitment to upholding the nation's integrity and rights.

The General Assembly yesterday issued a letter replying to the Capital's Anti-Japanese National Salvation Association, saying: "Having received your letter, we understand everything. Regarding your association's request to attend this meeting, it was submitted for discussion at the second meeting. It was agreed that the purpose of this meeting is for representatives of both sides to exchange views, and it is not appropriate for representatives from various sectors to participate. However, the various items discussed and decided at the meeting will be publicly disclosed in newspapers at any time for the reference of all sectors. We are responding with this letter, and hope you will take note of it." Addressed to the Capital's Anti-Japanese National Salvation Association, October 28th, Interim Chairman of the Meeting, Wang Zhaoming.

In the future, the direction and principles of foreign policy will be discussed and decided in this meeting, and then handed over to the Nanjing government for responsible negotiation. It can be said that the Beijing and Guangdong sides have completely converged on foreign policy steps. As for the rumored foreign affairs committee that is currently under discussion, due to today's resolution, there is naturally no need to establish it. Wang and Hu Talk to Representatives 104

The Capital's Anti-Japanese National Salvation Association sent representatives to Miles Road yesterday to see Mr. Hu Hanmin. At that time, Mr. Wang Jingwei was also at Mr. Hu's residence, so Wang and Hu met with the representatives at the same time. They both put forward opinions on the issues of peaceful reunification, foreign policy, and the restoration of the mass movement, and petitioned Wang and Hu. Regarding the issue of peaceful reunification, both stated that it was already being discussed in the peace conference and that there would be considerable results in the future. As for the issue of foreign policy, Mr. Hu earnestly told the representatives at the time that China may now have a solution only by implementing revolutionary diplomacy. As for the past foreign policy achievements, not to mention the warlord era, even since the establishment of the National Government in the sixteenth year of the Republic of China, we have talked about revolutionary diplomacy in words, but in practice, there is not much difference. Therefore, if we need to improve in the future, there must be a thorough reform. Then Mr. Wang spoke, saying that in the past, the Republic of China's politics, foreign policy, finance, and mass movement were all dominated by the military, so that everything could not develop freely. Therefore, what the Chinese people should strive for now is only to seek political liberation within the scope of the military. If this greatest goal can be quickly achieved, then all problems can be solved easily.

Wang Talks to Party Members 105

More than 20 party members from this city, including Wu Qiyu, Wang Zhisheng, and Jiang Hao, organized the Peace and Unity Promotion Association of Party Members in this city. Yesterday afternoon, they specially sent representatives Wang Zhisheng, Ge Hecai, Jiang Hao, Li Qiaozhi, Tang Wenquan, Wu Qiyu, and others to call on Mr. Wang Jingwei. The record of his conversation is as follows: (1) The representatives offered their opinions, hoping that this peace would be a revolutionary peace. After the peace, the party, government, and military must be thoroughly reformed. In terms of foreign policy, revolutionary diplomacy must be vigorously implemented. Wang replied, saying that he very much agreed with your opinions. Today's peace conference has decided that the Nanjing side will still be responsible for conducting foreign policy, but the principles and guidelines will be jointly decided by both sides. (2) The representatives asked about the results of today's peace conference. Wang replied that the meeting had not yet discussed internal affairs, but personally, I believe that at a minimum, the military and government must be separated before peaceful reunification is possible. If politics is still dominated by military forces, then there is absolutely no hope for political clarity, and democratic forces will have no way to establish themselves. (3) The representatives expressed that there is no freedom of speech and that the opinions of all sectors cannot be expressed. They hoped that the peace conference could first restore freedom of speech. Wang replied that he would do his best to do so.

Japanese Marines Land in Pudong Yesterday 109

Seized Japanese Goods, Red Bricks

But Were Cleverly Justified and Returned

The Situation at the Time Was Dangerous

Request to Lodge a Protest

According to a confidential report, the Anti-Japanese Association's Pudong inspection unit learned yesterday morning that five barges of red bricks sold by a Japanese person to a Chinese factory to build a chimney were sailing on the Huangpu River. At a time when the economic severance with Japan is so tense, the factory has forgotten that the country has been invaded by the violent Japanese and purchased a large number of bricks, which is unacceptable to the people. The unit immediately dispatched several inspectors to intercept the five barges of red bricks and escort them to the Hongsheng Wharf in Pudong, preparing to unload them into the nearby Yuanchang Warehouse for temporary storage, and then submit a report for consideration and punishment. Unexpectedly, at noon, a Japanese person, claiming to be Masuda Yuto, a representative of the Japanese firm Arai Yoko, arrived at the scene and forcibly demanded that the goods be returned to the inspectors. The inspectors immediately informed him that the goods had already been purchased by a Chinese person, and the goods belonged to the Chinese person and foreigners should not intervene. If there is a reason to disagree, he can negotiate with the General Association. However, the Japanese person repeatedly demanded and begged softly, and the inspectors ignored him because they saw that he could not be persuaded reasonably. They hired laborers to move the goods to the wharf and waited to put them into the warehouse. Unexpectedly, at 2:00 PM, the Japanese person returned with more than 20 fully armed marines from the Japanese Ataka warship, who arrived at the wharf on a small gasoline boat. All the guns were bayoneted, and they stabbed the laborers who were carrying the goods. The laborers were all empty-handed and had to dodge. Some who walked a little slower were stabbed in the legs by the Japanese soldiers' bayonets. The Japanese soldiers spread out guards on both sides of Pengjia Road and Dongchang Road for more than 20 feet, preventing pedestrians from passing by, as if facing a formidable enemy. Zhang, the district chief of the Third District Public Security Bureau, was informed and immediately led armed policemen to investigate and first questioned the Japanese soldiers why they landed with weapons and said that if there was a reason, they should follow the proper procedures. The Japanese soldiers had nothing to say. The district chief ordered them to return to the warship and sent representatives to explain. An officer named Dai Bang ordered the soldiers to board the ship first and accompanied the Arai representative to Chen, the district chief, saying that the red bricks were sold to the Japanese-owned Neiwai Cotton Mill in Xiaoshadu and were not purchased by a Chinese person. The district chief then allowed the return and instructed the inspectors that if they found that the Japanese bricks were transported in by a Chinese factory, they would be seized. A storm was finally over. Afterwards, District Chief Zhang reported the situation to the General Bureau and lodged a serious protest with the Japanese consul. The inspection station also reported the details to the Anti-Japanese Association. The Standing Committee of the Association immediately resolved: (1) to ask the municipal government to lodge a serious protest, and (2) to send a letter to the factory to inquire and ask for a reply.

Stop Supplying Japanese Merchants with Raw Lacquer Materials 112

Severely Punish Lacquer Merchants Chen Yutai and Others

The Anti-Japanese National Salvation Association of this city sent a letter to the Hankou Anti-Japanese Association yesterday, saying: "According to a confidential report, the raw lacquer produced in our country is a natural specialty, especially necessary for industry. The Japanese are cunning and good at imitating, and because of the relationship between weather and geography, they cannot cultivate or imitate it. Every year, the price of lacquer transported to Japan from our country reaches two to three million yuan, accounting for more than 60% of our annual production value. The reason why they need such a huge amount is for the cotton mills, which are necessary for industry. In recent years, Japanese yarn has been sold well all over the world. The wooden tubes used to manufacture 40-count fine yarn must be soaked in boiling water. If the lacquer does not have good durability, the manufacturing ability will be lost. If we can stop the supply of lacquer, we can control the life of Japanese yarn. Now that the new lacquer is about to be released on the market, it is the time to sever economic relations with the Japanese. There is no reason to supply Japanese merchants. However, the merchants in Hankou, such as Chen Yutai, Tong Qixiang, Xinhefu, Liu Yucheng, Yongchang, Chen Wanmei, Yiyuan Chang, Liu Yisheng, Liu Xietai, and Liu Yusheng are willing to please foreigners and have no love for the country, only caring about increasing prices to seek private gain. They still secretly provide the Japanese with new lacquer to Kato, Mizuta, and Tajima, with more than 1,000 pieces being transported to Shanghai to be loaded on ships for export. Now that the Japanese are rampant, when the whole country is determined to resist Japan, these traitors dare to violate public opinion and privately supply the enemy. This is deeply hated. Therefore, we request your association to consult with the Hankou Anti-Japanese Association to investigate and severely punish them to warn the wicked and extend popular outrage. In addition to Hankou, Yichang, Shashi, and Chongqing also have Japanese merchants who go to the interior to purchase new goods every time they are released on the market. Inland merchants have limited knowledge and cannot avoid being lured by profit. We also ask you to consult with the anti-Japanese organizations in these places to strictly prevent and block them. The situation reported is consistent and should be delivered immediately. Please investigate and handle it, and we hope to see a reply." Addressed to the Hankou Anti-Japanese Association.

Dalian Beans Should Be Allowed to Pass 114

The Municipal Chamber of Commerce Should Be Informed That Domestic Dalian Beans Should Be Allowed to Be Sold. Yesterday, It Telegraphed the Yongjia Anti-Japanese National Salvation Association, Saying: "To the Yongjia Anti-Japanese National Salvation Association, On the 27th of this month, according to a letter from the Shanghai Miscellaneous Grain, Oil Cake Industry Association, the letter from our colleague Qianlai Company said that Dalian beans are produced in the Northeast and are purely domestic goods, without any doubt. Therefore, the transportation and resale are not subject to any interference. However, recently, the Wenzhou Anti-Japanese Association, with a paper strip with the word "Showa" written on the bag, was mistaken for Japanese goods, and was immediately detained and prohibited from being sold. This is a misunderstanding. We are specially examining the two telegrams from the Wenzhou Chamber of Commerce and requesting that they be forwarded to the Wenzhou Chamber of Commerce to clarify the facts in order to correct them and facilitate business. The letter from our colleague Xinfeng Company is roughly the same as the previous one and is attached with the telegram from the Wenzhou Bean and Rice Industry Association. According to this, it is found that Dalian beans are purely domestic products and there is no doubt that the paper strips in the bags are originally used to prove the quality of the goods and have no other function. However, the Wenzhou Anti-Japanese Association regarded the word "Showa" on the storage slip as Japanese goods and detained them, which is a misunderstanding. We are urgently inspecting the original three telegrams and sending a letter to your association to quickly forward the telegram to the Wenzhou Anti-Japanese Association to explain the misunderstanding and release them immediately. In the future, do not leave any difficulties for Dalian beans in order to facilitate business and avoid disputes. According to this, the beans shipped from Dalian are known to be special products of our Northeast, but Dalian is within the sphere of influence of the Japanese. All the beans shipped out must be inspected by the exchange there before they can be shipped. The paper bag with the word "Showa" printed on it is the mark of the exchange's inspection and has no other meaning. Therefore, it cannot be assumed that the word "Showa" on the inspection is similar to a Japanese name and is considered a Japanese product. According to the report, we are sending a telegram to your association to ask you to examine it and immediately return all the beans and do not make it difficult for the beans to be transported and sold in the future. The Shanghai Municipal Chamber of Commerce is grateful and prints it."

Anti-Japanese Sound in Shipping News 115

Stopping the Loading of Japanese Goods to Tianjin Since the boycott, the Yangtze River

Page 10

The loading of Japanese goods has been stopped in the region, and the Japanese goods in the Beiyang region can still be used. The Japanese ships Longping, Kyozaki, Chohei, and Tangshan, etc., operating in this port still load and leave as usual. Therefore, in the past two months, Japanese goods from Shanghai to North China have still been exported. Until yesterday, the Japanese shipping companies in this port received a telegram from Tianjin that Jingu would not allow Japanese goods to be loaded and unloaded, and the workers would stop handling them. Please stop loading by various Japanese ships. Therefore, from today onwards, the Japanese ships going to Tianjin from Shanghai dare not load Japanese goods, fearing that they will not be able to unload after arriving at the port, which will limit the navigation of the ships.

Reduction of Sino-Japanese Postal Ships 116

There are a total of nine Sino-Japanese ships of the Japanese Post Office in this port. In peacetime, there were the most goods and passengers to and from, and the business was particularly prosperous. Therefore, four temporary ships were often added to operate. Since the boycott, the number of Japanese goods coming to Shanghai has been greatly reduced. The Japanese ships of the Japanese Post Office only loaded a part of American cotton, and there was nothing else. The company received a telegram from Japan yesterday saying that ships such as Tenjo Maru and Tsukuba Maru have been suspended from sailing immediately. Other ships can only reluctantly sail because the Japanese government has subsidies, but each trip will lose one or two thousand yuan.

Anti-Japanese Work in All Sectors 117

The Patriotic Barging Industry Association of the Japanese Barging Company has sent people to various wharves to promote and persuade all boatmen not to load Japanese goods again. The Japanese goods inspection team of the Seventh District Branch of the Citizens' Association, led by Liu Zhongying and Zhou Fuzhang, etc., inspected Japanese goods door-to-door in the Broadway Road area yesterday morning. A total of more than 80 shops were inspected, including Bailey, Commercial, Meitai, Zheng Deshun, Yutai, Zhongda, Xinda, Lihua, Taifeng, Shunchang, Huamei, Yishenchang, Yang Jinrong, Jingda, Dada, Shanghai Catering Company, Shangfa, Dedarong, Songmao, Shangde, Fuxing, Huada, Xintai, Zifeng, Dexiang, Dinghe, Dachang, Wu Fuli, Asia, Hongli, and Xinyi. It is heard that the team will continue to inspect door-to-door in the Hongkou area in the coming days.

All Staff of Huashang Electric Company Went on Strike 120

Due to the Long Delay in Resolving Treatment Conditions

But Electricity and Trams Are Still Supplied as Usual

All the staff of the Huashang Electric Company in this city went on strike at 9:00 AM yesterday due to the obstruction of Wu Quesheng, the chief of the general affairs section, in resolving the treatment conditions. However, trams and electricity are still running and supplied as usual. The various situations are recorded as follows:

Reasons for the Strike 121

All the staff of the Huashang Electric Company had requested to improve their treatment conditions and had submitted conditions. After repeated mediation by party and government agencies, a solution was possible. However, because Wu Quesheng, the chief of the general affairs section of the company, obstructed it, the solution was delayed and there was no way to resolve it. The representatives of all the staff had no choice but to resign to the public. All the staff decided to go on strike to promote awareness. Therefore, starting at 9:00 AM yesterday, all the staff of the lamp affairs, car affairs, general affairs, general affairs, materials, technology, engineering, accounting, and document sections went on strike. However, the staff managed to maintain trams and lights to ensure public services and social security.

Staff Conditions 122

In order to maintain order, all staff organized a maintenance committee and elected Ding Hanqing, Ding Jianshi, Lin Yiyun, Ma Chenglong, Zhang Yinzhi, Wang Juncai, Xu Shijun, Du Chengen, Zhan Chengxiang, Yang Siyuan, Wu Youren, Zhou Yongfang, Zhang Wenheng, Wang Jiaxiang, and Shao Changchun as the persons in charge. Therefore, the order was very good yesterday. According to the resolution of the general assembly, (1) Wu Quesheng, who sabotaged labor-management cooperation, was expelled, and (2) the amended conditions of the municipal party department were fulfilled. If the goal is not achieved, they will not work.

Representative Resignations 123

Urgent Statement from the Representatives of All Employees of the Chinese Merchants' Electric Company, Resigning Their Positions: We, the entire staff of the Chinese Merchants' Electric Company, requested that the company improve our treatment. The Social Affairs Bureau repeatedly, along with the Municipal Party Headquarters and the Public Utilities Bureau, dispatched personnel to convene talks between labor and management to mediate. The representatives, considering the impending national crisis, hoped for an early resolution and unity against external threats, and thus made concessions step by step, all of which are recorded and verifiable. On the 17th of this month, at 1:00 PM, the Social Affairs Bureau again, along with representatives from the Municipal Party Headquarters and the Public Security Bureau, convened talks between labor and management. The Director of the Social Affairs Bureau, Director Pan, personally handled the matter, and on the spot, the conditions for improved treatment proposed by the employees were discussed and decided upon item by item. These were recorded on the spot by Zhang Zhenyuan, a clerk from the Social Affairs Bureau committee, and representatives from the Municipal Party Headquarters and the Public Security Bureau were responsible for providing testimony. The representatives believed that the issue of improved treatment, which had been in dispute for half a year, could thus be considered concluded. Unexpectedly, on October 23rd, the Social Affairs Bureau issued an order and a set of implementation measures for the treatment, which completely altered all the clauses agreed upon at that time, completely inconsistent with the original agreement. Upon seeing this document, all the employees were extremely indignant and questioned the representatives, inquiring about the outcome of the previous discussions and the reported results, and why they were so different from the measures approved by the Bureau this time. Impatient individuals even denounced the representatives, questioning their credibility and character. The representatives, bearing this undeserved grievance, were unable to defend themselves. Regarding the Social Affairs Bureau's failure to follow the agreed-upon clauses, without consulting the employee representatives and the Municipal Party Headquarters, and arbitrarily altering the treatment measures, the representatives absolutely cannot recognize them and hereby resign from their representative positions to apologize to all the employees. All subsequent proceedings and matters will be directly discussed and handled by all the employees. The representatives bear no further responsibility. We hereby solemnly declare: Shao Shuping, Song Zhonghe, Sun Zhifei, Tan Zitang, Zhu Yan, Shen Yulin, Liu Xuekun, Zhu Wenlong, Shen Yuping, Du Ning, together.

Authorities Intervene 124

The Municipal Social Affairs Bureau issued an order yesterday to stop the matter, stating: In compliance with the order, it is reported that the employees suddenly went on strike en masse on the 28th of this month and misunderstood the Bureau's decision on treatment measures, openly slandering the Bureau, which is extremely inappropriate. Upon investigation, the measures decided by the Bureau were a compromise reached after assessing the situation of both parties. If the employees have any grievances, they can file an appeal with the Municipal Government, which is the proper procedure. However, during this time of national crisis, they have resorted to strikes as a means of coercion, which is a deliberate violation of the law. It is hereby ordered that work be resumed immediately and that an appeal be filed directly with the government, without further insistence, to avoid incurring blame. This order is imperative.

Report to the Municipal Government 125

The Municipal Social Affairs Bureau submitted a report to the Municipal Government yesterday, stating: Report on the matter of petitioning. This Bureau received a report stating that Deng Shuping and other employees of the Chinese Merchants' Electric Company suddenly went on strike on the 28th of this month and publicly published a statement slandering the government. Upon investigation, a dispute arose over the employees' request for the company to improve their treatment. This Bureau, together with relevant agencies, repeatedly dispatched personnel to convene interviews and impartially decided on nine measures to resolve the points of contention between the two parties, and separately ordered compliance, which was submitted to Your Excellency's government for approval and filing. Now, after reading the published statements of the employees, they stated, "Director Pan personally handled the matter, and on the spot, the conditions for improved treatment proposed by the employees were discussed and decided upon item by item." "Unexpectedly, upon issuing the order and the implementation measures for the treatment, all the clauses agreed upon at that time were completely altered, completely inconsistent with the original agreement," etc. This is greatly misunderstood in comparison to the situation in which separate advice was given at the time. The employees' requests were only for the Director's reference in advising the management, and conversely, the management's statements were also only for the Director's reference in advising the labor side. There was absolutely no agreement reached with either party under the form of conversation. The details are all recorded and verifiable. However, it is heard that the employees are dissatisfied with the fact that the management did not agree to the salary increase in October, and the Bureau's decision was to start the increase in October of the 20th year. Regarding the amount of the salary increase, the employees are also dissatisfied with the level of "36 yuan or more, a 30% increase" in the two levels from 20 yuan or more to 50 yuan or more. This is hearsay, and what their true intention is has not been reported. In short, the Director handled this case as a dispute between the employees of a public utility and the company, and failed to mediate it according to the Law on Handling Labor Disputes. He only solicited the opinions of both parties, advised them accordingly, and sought a compromise solution in the midst of mutual contention. If the employees are dissatisfied with the decision, they can file another appeal. Now, they are inciting strikes and arbitrarily coercing, which is extremely inappropriate. Regarding the matter of the strike of public utility employees, it is appropriate to submit a written report on the handling of this case, together with a copy of the records of the repeated interviews, for Your Excellency's government to review and quickly convene both parties for a decision to avoid disputes. The entire set of records is also requested to be returned after the handling is completed, which is a matter of public convenience. Respectfully submitted.

Company Meeting 126

After all the employees of the Chinese Merchants' Electric Company went on strike, General Manager Lu Bohong convened a meeting of all section chiefs at 10:00 AM yesterday, and reported the details of the incident to the Public Utilities Bureau, the Social Affairs Bureau, and the Public Security Bureau for legal processing. At 7:00 PM, he convened a joint emergency meeting at the United Association headquarters on Beijing Road to discuss everything.

Thorough Investigation by Party and Government 127

After all the employees of the Chinese Merchants' Electric Company went on strike, the Municipal Party Headquarters was deeply concerned that the prolongation of the strike would affect the operation of streetcars and the activation of electricity, and would have a significant impact on social security and transportation. In order to find a way to resolve the situation quickly, it specially dispatched Zhao Bingchang, a cadre from the Civil Training Section, to conduct a thorough investigation of the truth and report it, so that it could be handled in conjunction with the Social Affairs Bureau. It is heard that the Social Affairs Bureau also sent Guo Yongxi to conduct a thorough investigation last night.

Worker Assistance 128

All the workers of the Chinese Merchants' Electric Company, in view of the fact that all the employees were subjected to unreasonable oppression by the management and had no choice but to go on strike automatically, expressed their assistance and willingness to serve as a backing. Last night, slogans were posted all over the streetcars: (1) Expel Wu Quesheng, (2) Assist the employees to victory, (3) All workers unanimously support the union, (4) Support all union directors and supervisors, (5) Implement treatment regulations and agreements.

Union Statement 129

Zhou Guangrong, the standing director of the First District Water and Electricity Industry, expressed his opinion to the Xin Sheng News Agency yesterday regarding the employee strike, saying that his union has absolutely no relationship with the Employee Friendship Association. Moreover, in the past, when workers had disputes over treatment conditions, the employees never assisted us. Therefore, the union will not provide assistance to the employees in this strike. However, all the workers, because Wu Quesheng undermined the labor movement, expressed their sympathy to the employees. This is an automatic action by the workers, and the union is trying to persuade them. If the employee strike is prolonged, it is feared that there will be no streetcar tickets for sale tomorrow.

Anti-Drug Association Protests Opium Planting in Fujian 134

Public Telegrams from Southern Fujian

Local Officials Force Planting and Tax Collection

The Chinese National Anti-Drug Association has received numerous telegrams and letters from public organizations in southern Fujian in recent days, reporting that local military and political personnel are sheltering opium seedlings and collecting land taxes. The Anti-Drug Association is deeply saddened. It is now compiling the facts and protesting to the central government and the Fujian provincial government, and plans to unite with various Fujian public organizations in Shanghai to urge them to quickly eradicate the opium and severely punish local officials who violate the prohibition laws. It is heard that the Xiamen National Anti-Drug Association has repeatedly sent telegrams to report, but they have been inspected and withheld by the local authorities, which shows the local authorities' guilt. Yesterday, another urgent telegram was received, the original text of which is as follows: To the Shanghai Chinese National Anti-Drug Association, it has recently been reported that Zhangzhou and Tong'an are planting opium seedlings on a large scale. Zhang Zhen went to the countryside to encourage planting, and the opium taxes are collected by the Finance Department and Chen Zhijun, Lin Zhe, and Chen Qiyu. Tong'an has subcontracted to Ye Xihuang and Battalion Commander Chen Kun at a price of 1.2 million yuan, nominally for field tax. Zhangzhou is nominally for tax deed fields, and the tax comes from opium seeds. Farmers are required to exchange cash. Zhangzhou has implemented a public sale of opium paste, which is contracted by Hong Zhemin, using the name of opium lamp tax. Each regiment of the military also distributes 100 taels of opium per month for sale. The opium seedlings in Quanzhou and Putian are definitely a cooperation between Fang Shengtao and Chen Guohui. We sincerely request that the central government severely punish them or send personnel to inspect them on the ground to clarify the truth. Sincerely, Xiamen Anti-Drug Association. In addition, various mass organizations of farmers, workers, merchants, and students from Jinjiang, Nan'an, and Anhai have also sent telegrams in recent days, requesting the Anti-Drug Association to request the government to quickly stop the opium seedlings. Excerpts from the telegrams are as follows: (1) Since last year, Nan'an, Hui'an, Datian, Yongchun, Dehua, Tong'an, and other counties have reserved poppies to collect opium, and Chen Guohui and Zhang Zhen have collected donations. This year is even worse. Now, the Tong'an County has dispatched Chen Kun's special task battalion to donate 1.2 million yuan with the county. Most of Nan'an, Jinjiang, Hui'an, and other places have planted. (2) Opium seedlings have been planted in Jinjiang, Nan'an, Anxi, Yongchun, Hui'an, Tong'an, and other counties this season. After the floods and wars, if we do not pay attention to the production of food crops, the local area will be disturbed. What will become of us? (3) The opium seedlings in southern Fujian have been planted this season, a hundred times more than last year. The provincial government has indeed collected donations for opium seedlings. The stationed army also verbally reported that the opium seedlings in Quanzhou will be donated this season, with 1.2 million yuan determined by merchants, and a special bureau has been established.

Land Bureau Announces Survey of 23 Bao in Yinxiang District 140

Owners of Various Businesses in 3 and 5 Countries Fill Out Forms

The Municipal Land Bureau issued an announcement yesterday, which read: Announcement, the Bureau is now beginning to survey the land in 23 Bao of Yinxiang District, 3 and 5 map households. All owners should pay attention to the following items: (1) The land guarantor will distribute the filing form to the owners. All owners should fill in the form truthfully within ten days after receiving it, and the land guarantor will collect it and submit it to the third survey team of the Bureau's survey team in the Jicheng Yarn Factory on Qiujiang Bridge on Jungong Road, or the owner can submit it directly to the survey team. (2) Anyone who has not received the filing form due to the owner's address being unknown can go directly to the Bureau or the third survey team to fill it out. (3) Any owner who cannot fill in the land deed account and mu points because the land deed is mortgaged should immediately copy it from the mortgagee and not refuse. (4) When the land of each household is surveyed, the owner must, together with the land guarantor, point out the boundaries of the four sides to the investigator or surveyor, or entrust a representative to point out the boundaries on the spot. Otherwise, the Bureau will only rely on the land guarantor's instructions. If any errors or disputes arise in the future, the owner will be responsible. The above four items are related to the owner's consolidated property rights. Please pay special attention to this announcement.

Shipping News 141

Jianghua Collides with Sand Boat The China Merchants Steam Navigation Company's Yangtze River liner Jianghua collided with a sand boat near Wuhu while en route from Hankou to Shanghai. The Jianghua needed to dock at the Wuhu wharf as usual. As the Jianghua was approaching the port, a sand boat was sailing in front of the Wuhu Customs. British Mail Ship Demolished 144

The British Company's first-class mail ship Middlesex No. 9, weighing 11,000 tons, arrived in Shanghai from London yesterday and will set sail for Japan today to be demolished. This ship has been in the Sino-British class for 27 years. During the European War, it was converted into a cruiser by the British government. Now that the British Company has built a new ship of 16,000 tons with strong speed in the Far East route to replace it, the mail ship has been abolished. This return to Shanghai is the last time.

Shanghai County Police Academy Held Inspection Yesterday 145

The first phase of police cadets in Shanghai County has long since graduated and been assigned to various district public security bureaus for apprenticeship. The second phase of police cadets is being actively trained. County Magistrate Yan believes that the police are an essential element in ensuring local security. Training is not considered to be too strict or comprehensive. Therefore, he usually pays great attention to the police training. Yesterday, the police cadets held an inspection. At 9:00 AM, all the police cadets, fully armed, gathered in the drill ground. At the sound of a bugle, the entire field stood in silence. First, a military parade was held. County Magistrate Yan inspected the entire team and walked around once. Then, the instructor gave the order to salute. All the police cadets paid their respects and paid attention. The military appearance was solemn and the movements were agile. Then, the order was issued to drill. The steps were neat. After the drill, County Magistrate Yan gave a speech, saying that the police have a close relationship with the people of society. If you do not cultivate your own personality, it is difficult to correct the bad habits of the people of society. The book says, "If one's own person is upright, he can rule without command; if his own person is not upright, even with command, he will not be obeyed." At this time of national crisis, it is even more important for everyone to cultivate their personality and work hard for the country. As a police officer, being able to fulfill one's responsibilities in one's own position is being a good police officer, which is the way to save the country. Then, Director Ye and Security Section Chief Yao Gongzhi spoke in succession. Then, they practiced judo, and Chief Inspector Xu led the entire team to set off for a parade. This Friday, the team will be led to Chenxing, Sanlintang, and other places to conduct field exercises.
